PREFACE.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1726300246789.jpg"/>

The following is a Popular Edition of the Hitopadesha of Bhatta N├вr├вyana containing full explanatory notes, a glossary of words and a literal translation of all the verses occurring in the text and the dissolution of compounds adapted to meet the requirements of the less advanced students. By a Popular edition is meant such a one as can be easily understood without the help of a teacher even by a student who has studied the first few lessons of the 2nd book of Sanskrit Series. It is thus hoped that it will be largely availed of by the generality of students and especially by those who study privately and for whom it is chiefly intended. An experience of some years as a teacher of Sanskrit has convinced the editor that a book of this kind now presented would be generally acceptable. Hence he thinks that the publication of the book meets a long-felt want. It is prepared on the model of the Five Tantras or Panchatantra, which has been before the public for the last 3 years.

No pains have been spared to make this book useful to those for whom it is intended.

Any suggestions as to the meaning of a particular passage or individual words will be deemed a favour.

THE EDITOR.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1726327494369.jpg"/>

** рез** What is the good of a son being born who is neither learned nor pious? Of what use is an eye that is blindтАФexcept that it is an eyesore? ** рез **A man of merit, be he the son of anybody, is respected. What can a bow, though made of the best bamboo, do, when it is (рдирд┐рд░реНрдЧреБрдг) stringless? ** рез** From avarice arises anger, from avarice is produced desire for pleasure, from avarice result infatuation and destruction ; avarice is the root of sin. ** рез** A friend who is a collyrium made of love to the eyes,. an object of delight to the mind, and who is a ‘fit ? receptacle of happiness and misery (sharing happiness and misery with his friend ), is very hard to find ; but ’ those other friends, who, full of the greed of money (surround you) in your days of prosperity, are to be found everywhere. ** рез** That man, who is moderate in his wishes, bold and wise and who always follows his master like his shadow and who will not hesitate ( рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкреЗрдд ) when ordered to do a thing, will dwell (i. e. is fit to dwell) in the palace of a king. рдЕрд▓реНрдкреЗрдЪреНрдЫреБрдГ рдЕрд▓реНрдкрдВ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдЗрддрд┐. реи On account of your entrance (into his presence) at an inopportune time. рей Will disrespect. рек Be it as you say. рел Still & servant ought, by all means, to be by the side of his lord. рем Not undertaking anything through the fear of failure or an undesirable result is the sign of a mean fellow or dastard. ** рез** For example. реи A horse, a weapon, a science, a lute, a speech, a man and a woman become fit or unfit according as they come in contact with a worthy or unworthy person. рей What is the good of a servant who, though devoted is weak and what is the use of him who is able but obnoxious? ** рез** This is not right or proper. реи Oh lord of the Earth, one should not, of one’s own accord, take any step whatever without informing the king of it, except to retaliate an injury or to ward off a difficulty. рдЕрдирд┐рд╡реЗрджреНрдп without telling. рдЖрдкрддреНрдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рддреНтАФрдЖрдкрджрдГ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН рд╖реж рддреж рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреНрд░=рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреН. рей. Oh king, a minister is like a gourd used as a water-pot, which lets out (parts with ) a little and lets in much (water); he who does not take care of a moment, is a fool and he who cares not for a couri ( рд╡рд░рд╛рдЯрдХ ) is poor. рдХрдордВрдбрд▓реВрдкрдордГ ( рдмреж) рдХрдордВрдбрд▓реБрдГ рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрдиреБрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдГ ( рдмреж ) рддрдиреБрдГ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп. рдмрд╣реБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ (рдмреж) рдмрд╣реБрдГ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп. рдХрд┐рдВрдХреНрд╖рдг lit. he who says, what is a moment? тАЭ and thus neglects it ; similarly рдХрд┐рдВрд╡рд░рд╛рдЯрдХрдГ рек That minister is always to be preferred who raises a fortune even out of a couri; the treasure of a king who is opulent is his life and not life itself. The meaning is, the treasure is more valuable to a king than his life itself, because it (treasure) is the source of all worldly happiness.рел More-over, a man does command obedience by (merely observing) family practices or other like means. A man without wealth is abandoned even by his wife; what of others? ( not to mention others )рдЕрдиреНрдпреИрдГ рдХреБрд▓рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реИрдГ Mere practices prevailing in the family (cannot win respect for him if he has got no wealth ). рдХрд┐рдВрдкреБрдирдГ is equal in sense to рдХрд┐рдореБ or рдХрд┐рдореБрдд, already explained.

** рез**All ministers who are prosperous are ever hard to be won over. This is the opinion (рдЖрджреЗрд╢рдГ) of great sages or seers viz., prosperity injuriously affects the moral sense (Affluence is a sure domoraliser). рдЖрджреЗрд╢instruction, advice. рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреА (рдЙрдкрдкрдж) рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдХреБрд░реБрддреЗ рдЗрддрд┐. ** рез**For example, see. реи Mode or manner. рей Better is the loss of one’s life or even the cutting off of one’s head, than one’s neglect of him who is desirous of committing the sin of usurping the dignity of his lord. рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдГ рд╖реж рддреж, рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ рдкрджрд╕реНрдп рдЖрд╡рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдГ рдПрд╡ рдкрд╛рддрдХрдВ рддрддреН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫреЛрдГ- рек Acting towards you in a manner unworthy of himself, that is, his conduct with respect to you is not as it should be. рел In our presence. рем Having censured your prosperous Majesty’s three powers-which are рдкреНрд░рднреБрд╢рдХреНрддрд┐, рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐ and рдордВрддреНрд░рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐, that is, the eminent position, energy and the power of good counsel рен Stood silent or quiet. рео рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдорд╛рддреНрдп … рджреЛрд╖рдГ It is indeed a fault that your Majesty, having left off all other ministers, has given this one alone (рд╕рдВрдЬреАрд╡рдХ) full powers. репWhen the minister and the king ( both ) becoms very proud Prosperity stands, planting her foot immovably ; but being unable to bear the burden through her weakness as a woman, she gives up one of two рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН рд╖реж рддреж рдПрдХрддрд░ one of two.

** рез** When a king makes some one minister the sole authority in the kingdom, pride takes possession of him through infatuation, and he separates from his master through the neglect of affairs caused by pride, and when separated, a desire for independence springs up in his bosom, and then through the desire of independence, he acts the traitor towards the king and wishes to deprive the king even of his life. рд╕реНрд╡рддрдВрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдкреГрд╣рд╛ рд╖реж рддреж. реи Nothing short of a total destruction in the case of rice smeared with poison, of a tooth loosened (in its socket) and of a wicked minister, is safe. рд╡рд┐рд╖рджрд┐рдЧреНрдз рддреГ. рдд. рдореБрдЦрдореН = рдореБрдЦрд╛рд╡рд╣рдореН рей That king who entrusts his wealth to a minister, will, when that minister is in calamity, find himself helpless like a blind man with- out a guide. рд╕рдЪрд┐рд╡рд╛рдпрддреНрддрд╛рдВ рд╖. рдд рддрджреНрд╡реНрдпрд╕рдиреЗ = рддрд╕реНрдп (рд╕рдЪрд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдп) рд╡реНрдпрд╕рдиреЗ рд╖. рдд.рек Of his own free will or pleasure.

** рез**One who is being drowned in the ocean and finds the support of a serpent, can neither forego it nor take hold of it; so bewildered am I (such is the nature of my bewilderment ) рд╕рд░реНрдкрд╛рд╡рд▓рдВрдмрдирдВ рд╖реж рддреж. ** рез**Let what befits the occasion be done. рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдХрд╛рд▓ is a Bahu. qualifying рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдореН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рдХрд╛рд▓рдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп реи It is indeed aptly said. рей It is not possible to ascertain from their conduct what the deeds of the wicked are not conversant with. рек Women are accessible to the wicked, and a king generally supports an unfit person, wealth follows the miserly and rainтАФGod sends down rain on mountains and eeas. рджреБрд░реНрдЬрдирдЧрдореНрдпрд╛ рддреГреж рддреж ; рдЕрдкрд╛рддреНрд░рднреГрддреН (рдЙрдкрдкрдж.) рдЕрдкрд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рдмрд┐рднрд░реНрддрд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреГрдкрдгрд╛рдиреБрд╕рд╛рд░рд┐тАФрдХреГрдкрдгрдВ рдЕрдирд╕рд░рддреАрддрд┐. рдЙрдкрдкрдж. рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рдЬрд▓рдзрд┐рд╡рд░реНрд╖реАтАФрдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рдЬрд▓рдзреНрдпреЛрдГ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рддреАрддрд┐.’ рдЙрдкрдкрдж. рел Some bad person appears good through the beauty of the thing he resorts to, just as the dirty collyrium appears bright when put into the eyes of young women. рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдпрд╕реМрдВрджрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН рд╖ рдд, рдкреНрд░рдорджрд╛рд▓реЛрдЪрдирдиреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдВ рд╕. рдд.рем What is there strange in the fact that a king though served with efforts, is not pleased? ** рез** But this is an inexplicable (рдкреНрд░рдореЗрдп) truth. рдЕрд╢рдХреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердГ (рдм.) рдЕрд╢рдХреНрдпрдГ рдЕрд░реНрдердГ рдпрд╕реНрдп реи He who becomes angry for some (definite) cause, is pacified when that cause is removed; but how will a man please him whose mind is full of hatred without any cause? рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рдгрджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рд┐ рдиреж рддреж (рди рдХрд╛рд░рдгрджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рд┐реж). рей Or rather рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ is used to correct a foregoing statement.рек Injuring others without any cause рдирд┐рд░реНрдЧрддрдВ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рддрдерд╛ рдЕрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдГ рел If some wise and sympathetic persons confer some obligation, it becomes hateful, while if others actually do any harm, it becomes pleasing; the conduct of those whose minds are full of various sentiments (ever changeful or fickle) is indeed very strange and capricious. The duty of servitude is very difficult and is impracticable even to sages. рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮреИрдГ (рдЙрдкрдкрджреж) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдВ рдЬрд╛рдирдВрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рддреИрдГ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮреИрдГ рдиреИрдХрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рди-( рдПрдХрднрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдпрд╛рдГ рдПрдХрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдВрд╢реНрд░рдпрд╛рдГ, рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдПрдХ рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ ).рем Hundreds of deeds are lost upon those who are wicked, hundreds of good sayings, upon those who are unwise, hundreds of precepts on those who are disobedient and hundreds of wise counsels, on those who are foolish or dull-headed рдХреГрдд=рдХреГрддреНрдпрдВ. рдЕрд╡рдЪрдирдХрд░реЗреж рди рдирд╡рдЪрдирдХрд░реЗ-рдиреж рддреж Similarly рдЕрд╕рддреНрд╕реБ, рдЕрдмреБрдзреЗрд╖реБ and рдЕрдЪреЗрддрдиреЗ.

** рез** True and false, harsh and sweet-speaking, cruel and merciful, greedy and bountiful, always spending and also obtaining wealth in large quantities-thus royal policy is of various forms like a harlot. рдЕрд░реНрдердкрд░рд╛ (рдм.) рдЕрд░реНрдердГ рдкрд░рдВ (рдкреНрд░рдзрд╛рдирдВ) рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╛рдГ; рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╡реНрдпрдпрд╛ (рдм.) рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рд╡реНрдпрдпрдГ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЪреБрд░рд░рддреНрди рдзрдирд╛рдЧрдорд╛-рдкреНрд░рдЪреВрд░рд░рддреНрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдЪ рдЖрдЧрдордГ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд╛, рдм. реи Restored to his own self, become himself again.рей At his ease. рек Let there be this in addition. рел Let рд╕реБрд╣реГрджреНрднреЗрджthere be in the houses of your enemies let the wicked being attacked by death, be destroyed from, day to day; let people be the recipients of every kind of happiness and prosperity, and let even children ever feel delight in these pleasant stories. рем Thus ends the 2nd collection of stories in Hitoadesha called, рд╕реБрд╣реГрджреНрднреЗрдж (breach of friendship or separation of friends).

** рез** A king should make that his minister who is born in his country, who is hereditary, very pure or pious, versed in the Vedic verses or in counselling, not addicted to any vices, free from the sin of adultery, conversant with the ways of the world, foremost, famous, learned and the producer of wealth. рд╡реНрдпрднрд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рд╡рд┐рд╡рд░реНрдЬрд┐рдд рддреГ. рдд., рдЕрдзреАрддрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрдердореН (рдм.) рдЕрдзреАрддрдГ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрдердГ рдпреЗрди. Here рдХреБрд▓рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реЗ for рдХреБрд▓рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рдВ gives better sense, as рдХреБрд▓рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реЗ is to be taken with рд╡рд┐рд╢реБрджреНрдзрдореН and meaning pure in family practices. реиAre comprehended or included in Jambudvipa. рейThere too, your majesty is supreme. рекA king, one who is intoxicated, a child, a careless person and one who is proud of his wealth-wish for that which is not obtainableтАУhow much more then do they do for that which can be obtained. рдзрдирдЧрд░реНрд╡рд┐рддрдГ рдкрдВ. рдд. or (рддреГ. рдд.) рдзрдирд╛рддреН рдзрдиреЗрди рд╡рд╛ рдЧрд░реНрд╡рд┐рддрдГ.релIf sovereignty is proved by mere words &c. рем Who goes as an emissary? ** рез** A messenger should be devoted, virtuous, pure, vigilant, bold, free from vices, forgiving, a Br├бhman, knowing the secrets or defects of others and of a corresponding disposition (рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рднрд╛рд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН ). The blackness of the deadly poison never goes away even by its contact with Isvara (Siva). The meaning seems to be that as blackness never leaves the deadly poison, so goodness or devotedness never leaves a Br├бhman. рей A wicked person commits a misdeed while its fruit is suffered by the good; R├бvana carried away Sit├б, while the great ocean suffered confinement (bridging) Here рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН = рдЖрд╕рд╛рддреН рек One should never live or go together with a wicked person, a swan who was sitting quiet was killed through his contact with a crow, and Vartaka who was going (also suffered).

** рез** Even favourable and agreeable things when uttered by the wicked, create fear, like the blossoming of untimely flowers. рдЕрдХрд╛рд▓ &c. рез At the inatigation of some one of our officers. реи A sick person is desirable to physicians, he who is vicious or he who is in danger, is so to government servants; a fool is the means of livelihood to the learned and one belonging to a good caste ( is the means of livelihood) to the good. ** рез**Before he blocks up the entrance to our рдпрд╛рд╡рддреНтАФ рддрд╛рд╡рддреН to be translated into English in this way. реи In the paths among rivers, mountains and forests. рей A king should destroy the army of his enemy, which is tired by a long journey, surrounded by rivers, hills and forests, frightened by the dread of a terrible fire, afflicted by hunger and thirst, careless, engaged in eating, suffering from disease and famine, not stationary, small in number, afflicted by showers of rain and wind, covered by mud, dust and water, greatly scattered and dispersed by thieves, рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╡рд░реНрддреНрдордкрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдкрдВ.рдд. рек A king should destroy his enemy’s army which is tired by keeping awake the whole night through fear of attack and is sleeping by day, and the soldiers in which are overtaken by sleep. рел At leisure. рем Friend, good sir. ** рез** As the aligator though terrible becomes easily conquerable when out of water; so the lion though powerful becomes as tame as a jackal when out of his forest. реи Having put forth his army, a king should make them fight and himself be looking on. Does not even a dog become as brave as the lion when accompained by his master (to encourage him) ? рей A terrible fight. рек Perform or do. рел When the garrison in a fort is unable to sustain a prolonged siege, when it is small in numbers, when its leaders are foolish and vicious, when it is not well protected and when the men in it are timid, it is said to bea calamity of the fort. рдореВрд░реНрдЦрд╡реНрдпрд╕рдирд┐рдирд╛рдпрдХрдВ рдореВрд░реНрдЦрд╛рдГ рд╡реНрдпрд╕рдирд┐рдирд╢реНрдЪ рдирд╛рдпрдХрд╛рдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп. рдм. also рднреАрд░реБрдпреЛрдзрдВ рд╡. рем These four are said to be the remedies for storming or capturing a fortress*, viz.*, treachery, a long siege, assault and desperate fighting. рен Even before the rise of the sun.

** рез** One should take a good counsel, display great valour, fight well, flee soon as best as one can, when an opportunity offers itself and should never waste time in deliberation. реи Through respect for me. рей Consent рек Let the enemy enter the fort along the path smeared with my flesh and blood, that is, the enemy cannot enter the fort so long as I live.рел A lord who is liberal, forbearing and appreciative is obtained with great difficulty; I know (think) that even a servant who is pure in conduct, vigilant and devoted is also hard to find. рем It is proper on one’s part to run away from the battle-field if by so doing there is no fear of death; if however, death is sure to befall a mortal, why should fame be sullied (by fleeing ) in vain?

рдЕрдиреНрдпрдЪреНрдЪред **^(рез)**рднрд╡реЗрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдкрд╡рдиреЛрджреНрднреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд╡реАрдЪрд┐рд╡рд┐рднреНрд░рдорднрдЩреНрдЧреБрд░реЗред

** рез** In this worldly existence which is as transitory as the sports of the waves agitated by the wind, the sacrifice of one’s life for the sake of others, happens only through great merit. рдкрд╡рди… рднрдВрдЧреБрд░реЗ qualifying рднрд╡реЗ. рдкрд╡рдиреЗрди рдЙрджреНрднреНрд░рд╛рдВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡реАрдЪреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рднреНрд░рдорд╡рддреН рднрдВрдЧреБрд░реЗ. реи Theking, ministers, the country, fort, treasure, army, friends or allies, subjects and the multitudes of citizens,тАУare the constituent parts of a kingdom. рейThe subjects, when without a king, do not live however prosperous they may be; what can even the most excellent physician do to one whose life has departed. рек The people die when the king dies, and when he prospers they prosper, just as a sun-lotus does ( contract and open at the setting and rising of the sun). The first рдирд┐рдореАрд▓рддрд┐ is loc. sing. of the pre. parti. рдирд┐рдореАрд▓рддреН. рел Concealed or protected by his own body.

**^(рен)**рдЗрддрд┐ рд╣рд┐рддреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢реЗ рд╡рд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣реЛ рдирд╛рдо рддреГрддреАрдпрдГ рдХрдерд╛рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГред

** рез** Bards whose duty it is to sing the praises of the king.реи Royal camp. рей All cows bring forth young ones having the shape of bulls, but hardly one among them produces the chief of bulls whose shoulder is scratched by his horns (this being considered a good sign). рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдгреЛ &c., is a рдм. рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЙрд▓реНрд▓рд┐рдЦрд┐рддреЛ рд╕реНрдХрдиреНрдзреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рек Those brave persons, who sacrifice their lives for their lord in battles and who are attached to him and are grateful, obtain heaven. рел Whenever a brave person is surrounded and killed by the enemy, he obtains the eternal worlds, provided he does not flee from the field of battle.рем May there be no battles among kings by means of their elephants, horses and infantry, and may their enemies take shelter in the caves of mountains, being struck as it were, by the winds in the shape of policy and counsel. ренThus ends the third collection of stories in the Hitopadesha called Hostility.

** рез** A child, an old man, one who is long sick, one who is out-casted, one who is timid, one whose servants are timid, one who is avaricious and also one whose servants are greedy, one whose ministers are disaffected, one who is excessively attached to pleasures, one who receives advice from many heads (people), one who censures gods and Br├бhmans; one whose fate is adverse, also one who relies on fate as all in all; one who is overtaken by the calamity. of scarcity, one who is troubled by a calamity to his army, one who does not stay in the country, one who has many enemies, one whose actions are not limited by time, one who swerves from the true religionтАФthese are the twenty persons. рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд┐рдмрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдХреГрддрдГ рддреГ. рдд; рднреАрд░реБрдЬрдирдХрдГ (рдмреж) рднреАрд░реБрдХрд╛рдГ рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп. ** рез** One should not do anything rashly; want of consideration is a great abode of miseries; for, wealth of itself seeks (lit. marries) him who does things consider- ately, being attracted by his qualities. реи Although four remedies have been enumerated for the accomplishment of an object, their use (lit. fruit) is only in the number, while real success lies in peace (the first of the four remedies). рей An ignorant person can be easily satisfied, while he who knows much can be more easily satisfied; but even Br├бhman does not (cannot) please him who is puffed up with pride by (possessing) a particle of knowledge. рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд▓рд╡рджреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджрдЧреНрдзрдВ рддреГ. рдд. рек By the observation of the business accomplished by him.рел Everywhere, the existence of virtues absent is to be inferred from the actions performed; the actions, therefore, of those who act, in our absence are, to be known by the fruit. рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдиреБрдореЗрдпрд╛ рддреГ. рдд, рдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖- рд╡реГрддреНрддреАрдирд╛рдВ (рдм.) рдкрд░реАрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╡реГрддреНрддрдпрдГ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ. рем Dispute, repartee.

^(рен)рдкрд░рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрдирдВ рдлрд▓рдВ рдпрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╕реНрдХрдиреНрдзреЗрди рджреАрдпрддреЗред

** рез** That in which a vow is made that by the chief warriors on our side our object will be accomplished, is called рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрддрд░. реи That in which an enemy makes a vow that тАЬyou alone will accomplish my purposeтАЭ is called рдЕрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрдкреБрд░реБрд╖. рейThat in which a powerful enemy is made peace with by the stake of a portion of land by those versed in peace, is called рдЖрджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯ. рек That in which friendship is made with one’s own army by giving away every thing for the sake of protecting life is called рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯ. рел That which is made for the sake of preserving the life of the respectable by the sacrifice of the whole treasure, a part or half of it, is called рдкрд░рд┐рдХреНрд░рдп. рем That which is made by giving away lands yielding substantial fruit is called рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрди, and that in which the whole produce derived from land is given away is called рдкрд░рднреВрд╖рдг. рен That in which a limited or fixed quantity of produce is given by being borne on the shoulders, is called рд╕реНрдХрдиреНрдзреЛрдкрдиреЗрдп peace by those versed in peace-making. рд╕рдВрдзрд┐рд╡рд┐рдЪрдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдГ рд╕. рдд.

^(рез)рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрддреБ рдореИрддреНрд░реА рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдХрд╕реНрддрдерд╛ред
рдЙрдкрд╣рд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮреЗрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪреИрд╡ рд╕рдВрдзрдпрдГреерезреирелрее

^(реи)рдПрдХ рдПрд╡реЛрдкрд╣рд╛рд░рд╕реНрддреБ рд╕рдВрдзрд┐рд░реЗрд╡ рдорддреЛ рдордоред

рез Mutual obligation, friendship, alliance and presentтАФthese four are said to beрд╕рдВрдзрд┐рд╜ or kinds of peace. реи(Of these four kinds) рдЙрдкрд╣рд╛рд░ (presents) is alone considered by me as real peace, all the other varieties of it are without friendship in them.рей Since a powerful invader does not return without obtaining any thing, any other peace than тАШpresent’ is not proper or desirable. рек What person will act against the rules of justice or morality for the body which is to perish either to-day or to-morrow through any disease or affliction ? рдЖрдзрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдзрд┐рдкрд░реАрддрд╛рдкрд╛рддреН рд╖ рдд рдзрд░реНрдордкрд┐рддрдВ рдЕреж рел The life of living beings is as unsteady as the reflection of the moon in water, having, therefore, known it to be so, one should always do what is beneficial. ремHaving known that this worldly existence is as transitory as the mirage, one should make friends with the good both for religion and happiness.

** рез** Opinion. реи One thousand horse-sacrifices and truth are considered equal (in merit), but truth is greater even than a thousand horse-sacrifices. рей In whom the ordeal of truth is the foremost. рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдзрд╛рдирдВ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдВ рдкреБрд░рдГрд╕рд░рдВ рдпрдпреЛрдГ рдмреж рек The different parts of royal policy. релMay peace be delightful to all victorious kings, may good people be free from miseries, may the fame of the good ever increase. May royal policy always remaining on the breast of ministers (in the minds) like a harlot kiss their mouths and may there be great festivity from day to-day.

** рез** So long as the moon-crested god (Shiva) remains dear to the daughter of the cold mountain (Him├бlaya); so long as Lakshm├о shines (gives delight to) in the heart of Mur├бri as does lightening in the clouds, so long as this golden mountain resembling a forest conflagration has the sun for its sparks, may this collection of stories composed by N├бr├бyana remain in existence.реи May this prosperous ruler as bright as the moon conquer his enemies, heтАФby whom this collection has been caused to be written and published. рейThus ends the 4th Collection of stories in Hitopadesha named (Sandhi) Peace. рек Here ends the Hitopadesha. рел May there be welfare.
